<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Adobe Flash</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p><b>Adobe Flash</b> (formerly called <b>Macromedia Flash</b> and <b>Shockwave Flash</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Multimedia" title="Multimedia">multimedia</a> <a href="/wiki/Computing_platform" title="Computing platform">software platform</a> for production of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_animations" title="Flash animations">animations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Browser_game" title="Browser game">browser games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rich_Internet_application" title="Rich Internet application">rich Internet applications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">desktop applications</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_application" title="Mobile application">mobile applications</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile games</a>. Flash displays text, <a href="/wiki/Vector_graphics" title="Vector graphics">vector</a> graphics and <a href="/wiki/Raster_graphics" title="Raster graphics">raster graphics</a> to provide animations, video games and applications. It allows streaming of <a href="/wiki/Flash_Video" title="Flash Video">audio and video</a>, and can capture mouse, keyboard, microphone and camera input.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_artist" title="Digital artist">Artists</a> may produce Flash graphics and animations using <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a>. <a href="/wiki/Software_developer" title="Software developer">Software developers</a> may produce applications and video games using <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Builder" title="Adobe Flash Builder">Adobe Flash Builder</a>, <a href="/wiki/FlashDevelop" title="FlashDevelop">FlashDevelop</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_Catalyst" title="Flash Catalyst">Flash Catalyst</a>, or any text editor when used with the <a href="/wiki/Apache_Flex" title="Apache Flex">Apache Flex</a> SDK.</p>
<p>End-users can view Flash content via <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Flash Player</a> (for web browsers), <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">AIR</a> (for desktop or <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">mobile apps</a>) or third-party players such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scaleform" title="Scaleform">Scaleform</a> (for video games). <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a> (supported on <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>) enables end-users to view Flash content using <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browsers</a>. <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Lite" title="Adobe Flash Lite">Adobe Flash Lite</a> enabled viewing Flash content on older <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a>, but has been discontinued and superseded by <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> programming language allows the development of interactive animations, video games, web applications, desktop applications and mobile applications. Programmers can implement Flash software using an IDE such as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Builder" title="Adobe Flash Builder">Adobe Flash Builder</a>, <a href="/wiki/FlashDevelop" title="FlashDevelop">FlashDevelop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Powerflasher_FDT" title="Powerflasher FDT">Powerflasher FDT</a>. <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a> enables full-featured desktop and mobile applications to be developed with Flash, and published for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Google Android</a>, and <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>.</p>
<p>Content-providers frequently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (June 2016)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> used to use Flash to display <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streaming video</a>, <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interactivity" title="Interactivity">interactive</a> multimedia content on <a href="/wiki/Web_page" title="Web page">web pages</a> and on Flash-enabled software. However, after the 2000s, the usage of Flash on Web sites declined;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Flash served primarily to build <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a> for mobile devices with Adobe AIR.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Websites">Websites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Websites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the early 2000s, Flash was widely installed on <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">desktop computers</a>, and was commonly used to display interactive <a href="/wiki/Web_page" title="Web page">web pages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Online_game" title="Online game">online games</a>, and to playback video and audio content.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifedeath_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-lifedeath-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2005, <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> was founded by former PayPal employees, and it used Flash Player as a means to display compressed video content on the web.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifedeath_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-lifedeath-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2000 and 2010, numerous businesses used Flash-based websites to launch new products, or to create interactive company portals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smash50_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-smash50-3">[3]</a></sup> Notable users include <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wildlife Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cartoon_Network" title="Cartoon Network">Cartoon Network</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">Disney</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smash50_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-smash50-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> After Adobe introduced hardware-accelerated 3D for Flash (<a href="/wiki/Stage3D" title="Stage3D">Stage3D</a>), Flash websites saw a growth of 3D content for product demonstrations and virtual tours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smash3d_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-smash3d-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, YouTube offered videos in <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> format to support the <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a>, which did not support Flash Player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifedeath_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-lifedeath-2">[2]</a></sup> After a <a href="/wiki/Apple_and_Adobe_Flash_controversy" title="Apple and Adobe Flash controversy">controversy with Apple</a>, Adobe stopped developing Flash Player for Mobile, focussing its efforts on <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a> applications and <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> animation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lifedeath_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-lifedeath-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2015, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_Inc." title="Google Inc.">Google</a> introduced <a href="/wiki/Google_Swiffy" title="Google Swiffy">Google Swiffy</a> to convert Flash animation to <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>, a tool Google would use to automatically convert Flash web ads for mobile devices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2015, YouTube switched to HTML5 technology on all devices, however it will preserve the Flash-based video player for older web browsers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RIAs">RIAs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: RIAs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After Flash 5 introduced <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> in 2000, developers combined the visual and programming capabilities of Flash to produce interactive experiences and applications for the Web.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flex3dummies_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-flex3dummies-11">[11]</a></sup> Such Web-based applications eventually came to be known as "Rich Internet Applications" (RIAs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flex3dummies_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-flex3dummies-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Builder" title="Adobe Flash Builder">Macromedia Flex</a> was released, and specifically targeted the application development market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flex3dummies_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-flex3dummies-11">[11]</a></sup> Flex introduced new <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a> components, advanced <a href="/wiki/Data_visualization" title="Data visualization">data visualization</a> components, data remoting, and a modern IDE (Flash Builder).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flex3dummies_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-flex3dummies-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvfb_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-dvfb-12">[12]</a></sup> Flex competed with <a href="/wiki/Ajax_(programming)" title="Ajax (programming)">Asynchronous JavaScript and XML</a> (AJAX) and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Silverlight" title="Microsoft Silverlight">Microsoft Silverlight</a> during its tenure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flex3dummies_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-flex3dummies-11">[11]</a></sup> Flex was upgraded to support integration with remote data sources, using <a href="/wiki/Action_Message_Format" title="Action Message Format">AMF</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlazeDS" title="BlazeDS">BlazeDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adobe_LiveCycle" title="Adobe LiveCycle">Adobe LiveCycle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Elastic_Compute_Cloud" title="Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud">Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud</a>, and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enterpriseflex_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-enterpriseflex-13">[13]</a></sup> As of 2015, Flex applications can be published for desktop platforms using <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flex3dummies_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-flex3dummies-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2006 and 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Speedtest.net" title="Speedtest.net">Speedtest.net</a> web service conducted over 9.0 billion speed tests using an RIA built with Adobe Flash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-test-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2016, the service shifted to <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> due to the decreasing availability of <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a> on PCs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2016, <a href="/wiki/Web_application" title="Web application">Web applications</a> and RIAs can be developed with Flash using the <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript 3.0</a> programming language and related tools such as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Builder" title="Adobe Flash Builder">Adobe Flash Builder</a>. Third-party <a href="/wiki/Integrated_development_environment" title="Integrated development environment">IDEs</a> such as <a href="/wiki/FlashDevelop" title="FlashDevelop">FlashDevelop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Powerflasher_FDT" title="Powerflasher FDT">Powerflasher FDT</a> also enable developers to create Flash games and applications, and are generally similar to <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Visual_Studio" title="Microsoft Visual Studio">Microsoft Visual Studio</a>. Flex applications are typically built using <a href="/wiki/List_of_Flex_frameworks" title="List of Flex frameworks">Flex frameworks</a> such as <a href="/wiki/PureMVC" title="PureMVC">PureMVC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enterpriseflex_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-enterpriseflex-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Browser_game" title="Browser game">Flash video games</a> are popular on the Internet, with portals like <a href="/wiki/Newgrounds" title="Newgrounds">Newgrounds</a> dedicated to hosting of Flash-based games. Popular games developed with Flash include <i><a href="/wiki/Angry_Birds" title="Angry Birds">Angry Birds</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Clash_of_Clans" title="Clash of Clans">Clash of Clans</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/FarmVille" title="FarmVille">FarmVille</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/AdventureQuest" title="AdventureQuest">AdventureQuest</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Machinarium" title="Machinarium">Machinarium</a></i>.</p>
<p>Adobe introduced various technologies to help build video games, including <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a> (to release games for desktop or mobile platforms), <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Scout" title="Adobe Scout">Adobe Scout</a> (to improve performance), <a href="/wiki/CrossBridge" title="CrossBridge">CrossBridge</a> (to convert C++-based games to run in Flash), and <a href="/wiki/Stage3D" title="Stage3D">Stage3D</a> (to support GPU-accelerated video games). 3D frameworks like <a href="/wiki/Away3D" title="Away3D">Away3D</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flare3D" title="Flare3D">Flare3D</a> simplified creation of 3D content for Flash.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a> allows creation of Flash-based <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile games</a>, which may be published to the <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Google Play</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> app stores.</p>
<p>Flash is also used to build interfaces and HUDs for 3D video games using <a href="/wiki/Scaleform_GFx" title="Scaleform GFx">Scaleform GFx</a>, a technology that renders Flash content within non-Flash video games. Scaleform is supported by more than 10 major video game engines including <a href="/wiki/Unreal_Engine" title="Unreal Engine">Unreal Engine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unreal_Development_Kit" title="Unreal Development Kit">UDK</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CryEngine_3" title="CryEngine 3">CryEngine</a> and <a href="/wiki/PhyreEngine" title="PhyreEngine">PhyreEngine</a>, and has been used to provide 3D interfaces for more than <a href="/wiki/List_of_games_using_Scaleform" title="List of games using Scaleform">150 major video game titles</a> since its launch in 2003.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_animation">Film and animation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Film and animation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Flash_animated_films" title="List of Flash animated films">List of Flash animated films</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Flash_animated_television_series" title="List of Flash animated television series">List of Flash animated television series</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a> is one of the common animation programs for low-cost 2D television and commercial animation, in competition with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anime_Studio" title="Anime Studio">Anime Studio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toon_Boom_Animation" title="Toon Boom Animation">Toon Boom Animation</a>.</p>
<p>Notable users of Flash include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DHX_Media_Vancouver" title="DHX Media Vancouver">DHX Media Vancouver</a> for productions including <i><a href="/wiki/Pound_Puppies_(2010_TV_series)" title="Pound Puppies (2010 TV series)">Pound Puppies</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/My_Little_Pony:_Friendship_is_Magic" title="My Little Pony: Friendship is Magic">My Little Pony: Friendship is Magic</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Fresh_TV" title="Fresh TV">Fresh TV</a> for <a href="/wiki/Total_Drama" title="Total Drama">Total Drama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nelvana" title="Nelvana">Nelvana</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/6teen" title="6teen">6teen</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Clone_High" title="Clone High">Clone High</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Williams_Street" title="Williams Street">Williams Street</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Metalocalypse" title="Metalocalypse">Metalocalypse</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Squidbillies" title="Squidbillies">Squidbillies</a></i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_Animation_Studios" title="Nickelodeon Animation Studios">Nickelodeon Animation Studios</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Wow!_Wow!_Wubbzy!" title="Wow! Wow! Wubbzy!">Wow! Wow! Wubbzy!</a></i> <i><a href="/wiki/El_Tigre:_The_Adventures_of_Manny_Rivera" title="El Tigre: The Adventures of Manny Rivera">El Tigre: The Adventures of Manny Rivera</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Danny_Phantom" title="Danny Phantom">Danny Phantom</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Happy_Tree_Friends" title="Happy Tree Friends">Happy Tree Friends</a></i><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Is there any evidence Nickelodeon Animation Studios produces Happy Tree Friends? (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, and more.</p>
<p>Flash is less commonly used for feature-length animated films; however, 2009's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_of_Kells" title="The Secret of Kells">The Secret of Kells</a></i>, an Irish film, was animated primarily in Adobe Flash, and was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Animated_Feature" title="Academy Award for Best Animated Feature">Academy Award for Best Animated Feature</a> at the <a href="/wiki/82nd_Academy_Awards" title="82nd Academy Awards">82nd Academy Awards</a>.</p>
<p>Several popular online series are currently produced in Flash, such as the <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a>-winning <i><a href="/wiki/Mike_%26_Mike" title="Mike &amp; Mike">Off-Mikes</a></i>, produced by <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> and <a href="/wiki/Animax_Entertainment" title="Animax Entertainment">Animax Entertainment</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Gotham_Girls" title="Gotham Girls">Gotham Girls</a></i>, produced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warner_Brothers" title="Warner Brothers">Warner Brothers</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Crime_Time" title="Crime Time">Crime Time</a></i>, produced by <a href="/wiki/Future_Thought_Productions" title="Future Thought Productions">Future Thought Productions</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Homestar_Runner" title="Homestar Runner">Homestar Runner</a></i> produced by <a href="/wiki/The_Brothers_Chaps" title="The Brothers Chaps">Mike and Matt Chapman</a>.</p>
<p><a href="#Third-party_tools">Various third-party software packages</a> designed for traditionally trained cartoonists and animators can publish animations in the <a href="/wiki/SWF" title="SWF">SWF</a> format.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FutureWave">FutureWave</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: FutureWave">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The precursor to Flash was a product named SmartSketch, published by <a href="/wiki/FutureWave_Software" title="FutureWave Software">FutureWave Software</a>. The company was founded by <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Jackson_(software)" title="Charlie Jackson (software)">Charlie Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Gay" title="Jonathan Gay">Jonathan Gay</a>, and Michelle Welsh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hs_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-hs-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfb_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-mfb-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bh1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-bh1-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bh2_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-bh2-20">[20]</a></sup> SmartSketch was a vector drawing application for pen computers running the <a href="/wiki/PenPoint_OS" title="PenPoint OS">PenPoint OS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> When PenPoint failed in the marketplace, SmartSketch was ported to <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classic_Mac_OS" title="Classic Mac OS">Mac OS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfb_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-mfb-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Back_to_Graphics_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Back_to_Graphics-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the Internet became more popular, FutureWave realized the potential for a vector-based web animation tool that might challenge <a href="/wiki/Macromedia" title="Macromedia">Macromedia</a> <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Shockwave" title="Adobe Shockwave">Shockwave</a> technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hs_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-hs-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfb_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-mfb-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1995, FutureWave modified SmartSketch by adding frame-by-frame animation features and released this new product as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">FutureSplash Animator</a> on Macintosh and PC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hs_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-hs-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfb_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-mfb-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Dawn_of_Web_Animation_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Dawn_of_Web_Animation-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>FutureWave approached <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe Systems</a> with an offer to sell them FutureSplash in 1995, but Adobe turned down the offer at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfb_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-mfb-18">[18]</a></sup> Microsoft wanted to create an "online TV network" (<a href="/wiki/MSN_Dial-up#MSN_2.0" title="MSN Dial-up">MSN 2.0</a>) and adopted FutureSplash animated content as a central part of it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfb_18-5"><a href="#cite_note-mfb-18">[18]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney_Online" title="Disney Online">Disney Online</a> used FutureSplash animations for their subscription-based service Disney's Daily Blast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hs_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-hs-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfb_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-mfb-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox Broadcasting Company</a> launched <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a> using FutureSplash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfb_18-7"><a href="#cite_note-mfb-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Macromedia">Macromedia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Macromedia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 1996, FutureSplash was acquired by Macromedia, and Macromedia re-branded and released <i>FutureSplash Animator</i> as <i>Macromedia Flash 1.0</i>. Flash was a two-part system, a graphics and animation editor known as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Macromedia Flash</a>, and a player known as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Macromedia Flash Player</a>.</p>
<p><i>FutureSplash Animator</i> was an animation tool originally developed for pen-based computing devices, but due to the small size of the <i>FutureSplash Viewer</i>, it was particularly suited for download over the Web. Macromedia distributed Flash Player as a free browser <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_(computing)" title="Plug-in (computing)">plugin</a> in order to quickly gain market share. As of 2005, more computers worldwide had the Flash Player installed than any other Web media format, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Java_Platform" title="Java Platform">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/QuickTime" title="QuickTime">QuickTime</a>, <a href="/wiki/RealNetworks" title="RealNetworks">RealNetworks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Player" title="Windows Media Player">Windows Media Player</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flash_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-flash-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Macromedia upgraded the Flash system significantly from 1996 to 1999, adding MovieClips, Actions (the precursor to <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a>), Alpha transparency, and other features. As Flash matured, Macromedia's focus shifted from marketing it as a graphics and media tool to promoting it as a <a href="/wiki/Web_application" title="Web application">Web application</a> platform, adding scripting and data access capabilities to the player while attempting to retain its small footprint.</p>
<p>In 2000, the first major version of ActionScript was developed, and released with <i>Flash 5</i>. Actionscript 2.0 was released with <i>Flash MX 2004</i> and supported <a href="/wiki/Object-oriented_programming" title="Object-oriented programming">object-oriented programming</a>, improved UI components, and other advanced programming features. The last version of Flash released by Macromedia was <i>Flash 8</i>, which focused on graphical upgrades such as filters (blur, drop shadow, etc.), blend modes (similar to <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Photoshop" title="Adobe Photoshop">Adobe Photoshop</a>), and advanced features for <a href="/wiki/Flash_Video" title="Flash Video">FLV video</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adobe">Adobe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Adobe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Macromedia was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe Systems</a> in 2005, and the entire Macromedia product line including Flash, <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Dreamweaver" title="Adobe Dreamweaver">Dreamweaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Director" title="Adobe Director">Director</a>/<a href="/wiki/Adobe_Shockwave" title="Adobe Shockwave">Shockwave</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Authorware" title="Authorware">Authorware</a> is now handled by Adobe.</p>
<p>In 2007, Adobe released <i>Adobe Flash CS3 Professional</i>, the first version released under Adobe, and the ninth major version of Flash. It introduced the <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript 3.0</a> programming language, which supported modern programming practices and enabled business applications to be developed with Flash. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adobe_Flex_Builder" title="Adobe Flex Builder">Adobe Flex Builder</a> (built on <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_(software)" title="Eclipse (software)">Eclipse</a>) targeted the enterprise <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">application development</a> market, and was also released the same year. Flex Builder included the Flex SDK, a set of components that included charting, advanced UI, and data services (<i>Flex Data Services</i>).</p>
<p>In 2008, Adobe released the historic tenth version of Flash, <i>Adobe Flash CS4</i>. Flash 10 improved animation capabilities within the <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Flash editor</a>, adding a motion editor panel (similar to <a href="/wiki/Adobe_After_Effects" title="Adobe After Effects">Adobe After Effects</a>), <a href="/wiki/Inverse_kinematics" title="Inverse kinematics">inverse kinematics</a> (bones), basic 3D object animation, object-based animation, and other advanced text and graphics features. <i>Flash Player 10</i> included the first in-built 3D engine (without GPU acceleration), that allowed basic object transformations in 3D space (position, rotation, scaling).</p>
<p>Also in 2008, Adobe released the first version of <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe Integrated Runtime</a> (later re-branded as <i>Adobe AIR</i>), a runtime engine that replaced Flash Player, and provided additional capabilities to the ActionScript 3.0 language to build desktop and mobile applications. With AIR, developers could access the file system (files &amp; folders), and connected devices (joystick, gamepad, sensors) for the first time.</p>
<p>In 2011, <i>Adobe Flash Player 11</i> was released, and with it the first version of <a href="/wiki/Stage3D" title="Stage3D">Stage3D</a>, allowing for GPU-accelerated 3D rendering for Flash applications and games, on desktop platforms such as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">Mac OS X</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Labrecque2011_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Labrecque2011-27">[27]</a></sup> Adobe further improved 3D capabilities from 2011 to 2013, adding support for 3D rendering on Android and iOS platforms, alpha-channels, compressed textures, <a href="/wiki/Texture_atlas" title="Texture atlas">texture atlases</a>, and other features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fproadmap_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-fproadmap-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Adobe AIR was upgraded to support 64-bit computers, and developers could now add additional functionality to the AIR runtime using <i>AIR Native Extensions</i> (ANE).</p>
<p>In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a> reached a milestone when over 100,000 unique applications were built on AIR, and over 1 billion installations of the same were logged from users across the world (May 2014).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Adobe AIR was voted as the <i>Best Mobile Application Development</i> product at the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a> for two consecutive years (CES 2014 and CES 2015).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FLA">FLA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: FLA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Flash source files are in the <a href="/wiki/SWF#Related_file_formats_and_extensions" title="SWF"><b>FLA</b> format</a>, and contain graphics and animation, as well as embedded assets such as bitmap images, audio files and FLV video files. The Flash source file format is a proprietary format and <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a> is the only available authoring tool capable of editing such files. Flash source files (.fla) may be compiled into Flash movie files (.swf) using Adobe Animate. Note that FLA files can be edited, but output (.swf) files cannot.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SWF">SWF</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: SWF">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/SWF" title="SWF">SWF</a></div>
<p>Flash movie files are in the <i>SWF</i> format, traditionally called "<b>S</b>hock<b>W</b>ave <b>F</b>lash" movies, "Flash movies", or "Flash applications", usually have a .swf <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/File_extension" title="File extension">file extension</a>, and may be used in the form of a web page plug-in, strictly "played" in a standalone Flash Player, or incorporated into a self-executing Projector movie (with the .exe extension in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>). <a href="/wiki/Flash_Video" title="Flash Video">Flash Video</a> files<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[spec 1]</a></sup> have a .flv file extension and are either used from within .swf files or played through a flv-aware player, such as <a href="/wiki/VLC_media_player" title="VLC media player">VLC</a>, or <a href="/wiki/QuickTime" title="QuickTime">QuickTime</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Player" title="Windows Media Player">Windows Media Player</a> with external <a href="/wiki/Codec" title="Codec">codecs</a> added.</p>
<p>The use of vector graphics combined with program code allows Flash files to be smaller—and thus allows streams to use less <a href="/wiki/Bandwidth_(computing)" title="Bandwidth (computing)">bandwidth</a>—than the corresponding bitmaps or video clips. For content in a single format (such as just text, video, or audio), other alternatives may provide better performance and consume less <a href="/wiki/Central_processing_unit" title="Central processing unit">CPU</a> power than the corresponding Flash movie, for example when using transparency or making large screen updates such as photographic or text fades.</p>
<p>In addition to a vector-rendering engine, the Flash Player includes a virtual machine called the ActionScript Virtual Machine (AVM) for scripting interactivity at run-time, with video, MP3-based audio, and bitmap graphics. As of Flash Player 8, it offers two video codecs: <a href="/wiki/On2_Technologies" title="On2 Technologies">On2 Technologies</a> <a href="/wiki/VP6" title="VP6">VP6</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sorenson_codec" title="Sorenson codec">Sorenson Spark</a>, and run-time <a href="/wiki/JPEG" title="JPEG">JPEG</a>, Progressive JPEG, <a href="/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics" title="Portable Network Graphics">PNG</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graphics_Interchange_Format" title="Graphics Interchange Format">GIF</a> capability. In the next version, Flash is slated to use a <a href="/wiki/Just-in-time_compilation" title="Just-in-time compilation">just-in-time</a> compiler for the ActionScript engine.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="3D">3D</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 3D">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stage3D" title="Stage3D">Stage3D</a></div>
<p>Flash Player 11 introduced a full 3D <a href="/wiki/Shader" title="Shader">shader</a> API, called <a href="/wiki/Stage3D" title="Stage3D">Stage3D</a>, which is fairly similar to <a href="/wiki/WebGL" title="WebGL">WebGL</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fisher2013_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fisher2013-35">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vs_webgl_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-vs_webgl-36">[35]</a></sup> Stage3D enables GPU-accelerated rendering of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3D_graphics" title="3D graphics">3D graphics</a> within Flash games and applications, and has been used to build <a href="/wiki/Angry_Birds" title="Angry Birds">Angry Birds</a>, and a couple of other notable games.</p>
<p>Various 3D frameworks have been built for Flash using Stage3D, such as <a href="/wiki/Away3D" title="Away3D">Away3D</a> 4,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vs_webgl_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-vs_webgl-36">[35]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CopperCube" title="CopperCube">CopperCube</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-develop-online-ccb4_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-develop-online-ccb4-37">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Flare3D" title="Flare3D">Flare3D</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gladstien2013_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gladstien2013-38">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Starling_Framework" title="Starling Framework">Starling</a>,.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Imbert2012_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Imbert2012-39">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:vii</sup> Professional game engines like <a href="/wiki/Unreal_Engine" title="Unreal Engine">Unreal Engine</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Au2012_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Au2012-40">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theverge_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-theverge-41">[40]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Unity_(game_engine)" title="Unity (game engine)">Unity</a> also export Flash versions which use Stage3D to render 3D graphics.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flash_Video">Flash Video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Flash Video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flash_Video" title="Flash Video">Flash Video</a></div>
<p>Virtually all browser plugins for video are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gratis#Software" title="Gratis">free of charge</a> and cross-platform, including Adobe's offering of Flash Video, which was first introduced with Flash version 6. Flash Video has been a popular choice for websites due to the large <a href="#Installed_user_base">installed user base</a> and programmability of Flash. In 2010, Apple publicly criticized Adobe Flash, including its implementation of video playback for not taking advantage of hardware acceleration, one reason Flash is not to be found on Apple's mobile devices. Soon after Apple's criticism, Adobe demoed and released a beta version of Flash 10.1, which takes advantage of GPU hardware acceleration even on a Mac. Flash 10.2 beta, released December 2010, adds hardware acceleration for the whole video rendering pipeline.</p>
<p>Flash Player supports two distinct modes of video playback, and <a href="/wiki/Video_codec" title="Video codec">hardware accelerated video decoding</a> may not be used for older video content. Such content causes excessive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CPU_usage" title="CPU usage">CPU usage</a> compared to comparable content played with other players.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Software Rendered Video</b> : Flash Player supports software rendered video since version 6. Such video supports vector animations displayed above the video content. This obligation may, depending on graphic <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">APIs</a> exposed by the operating system, prohibit using a <a href="/wiki/Video_overlay" title="Video overlay">video overlay</a>, like a traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_player_(application_software)" title="Media player (application software)">multimedia player</a> would use, with the consequence that <a href="/wiki/Color_space" title="Color space">color space conversion</a> and scaling must happen in software.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Hardware Accelerated Video</b> : Flash Player supports hardware accelerated video playback since version 10.2, for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H.264" title="H.264">H.264</a>, F4V, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FLV" title="FLV">FLV</a> video formats. Such video is displayed above all Flash content, and takes advantage of <a href="/wiki/Video_codec" title="Video codec">video codec</a> chipsets installed on the user's device. Developers must specifically use the "StageVideo" technology within Flash Player in order for hardware decoding to be enabled. Flash Player internally uses technologies such as <a href="/wiki/DirectX_Video_Acceleration" title="DirectX Video Acceleration">DirectX Video Acceleration</a> and <a href="/wiki/OpenGL" title="OpenGL">OpenGL</a> to do so.</li>
</ul>
<p>In tests done by <a href="/wiki/Ars_Technica" title="Ars Technica">Ars Technica</a> in 2008 and 2009, Adobe Flash Player performed better on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Windows" title="Windows">Windows</a> than <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">Mac OS X</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> with the same hardware.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Performance has later improved for the latter two, on Mac OS X with Flash Player 10.1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> and on Linux with Flash Player 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flash_Audio">Flash Audio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Flash Audio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Flash Audio is most commonly encoded in MP3 or AAC (<a href="/wiki/Advanced_Audio_Coding" title="Advanced Audio Coding">Advanced Audio Coding</a>) however it can also use <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ADPCM" title="ADPCM">ADPCM</a>, Nellymoser (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nellymoser_Asao_Codec" title="Nellymoser Asao Codec">Nellymoser Asao Codec</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Speex" title="Speex">Speex</a> audio codecs. Flash allows sample rates of 11, 22 and 44.1 kHz. It cannot have 48 kHz audio sample rate, which is the standard TV and DVD sample rate.</p>
<p>On August 20, 2007, Adobe announced on its blog that with Update 3 of Flash Player 9, Flash Video will also implement some parts of the <a href="/wiki/MPEG-4" title="MPEG-4">MPEG-4</a> international standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MP4_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-MP4-47">[46]</a></sup> Specifically, Flash Player will work with video compressed in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H.264" title="H.264">H.264</a> (MPEG-4 Part 10), audio compressed using <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Audio_Coding" title="Advanced Audio Coding">AAC</a> (MPEG-4 Part 3), the F4V, MP4 (MPEG-4 Part 14), M4V, M4A, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3GP" title="3GP">3GP</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/.mov" title=".mov">MOV</a> multimedia <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Container_format_(digital)" title="Container format (digital)">container formats</a>, <a href="/wiki/3GPP" title="3GPP">3GPP</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timed_Text" title="Timed Text">Timed Text</a> specification (MPEG-4 Part 17), which is a standardized subtitle format and partial parsing capability for the 'ilst' atom, which is the <a href="/wiki/ID3" title="ID3">ID3</a> equivalent <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> uses to store <a href="/wiki/Metadata" title="Metadata">metadata</a>. <a href="/wiki/MPEG-4_Part_2" title="MPEG-4 Part 2">MPEG-4 Part 2</a> and <a href="/wiki/H.263" title="H.263">H.263</a> will not work in F4V file format. Adobe also announced that it will be gradually moving away from the FLV format to the standard ISO base media file format (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MPEG-4_Part_12" title="MPEG-4 Part 12">MPEG-4 Part 12</a>) owing to functional limits with the FLV structure when streaming H.264. The final release of the Flash Player implementing some parts of MPEG-4 standards had become available in Fall 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Adobe Flash Player 10.1 does not have acoustic echo cancellation, unlike the VoIP offerings of Skype and Google Voice, making this and earlier versions of Flash less suitable for group calling or meetings. Flash Player 10.3 Beta incorporates acoustic echo cancellation.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scripting_language">Scripting language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Scripting language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a></div>
<p><i>ActionScript</i> is the programming language used by Flash. It is an enhanced superset of the <a href="/wiki/ECMAScript" title="ECMAScript">ECMAScript</a> programming language, with a classical Java-style class model, rather than JavaScript's prototype model.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications">Specifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Specifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 1998, Macromedia disclosed the Flash Version 3 Specification on its website. It did this in response to many new and often semi-open formats competing with SWF, such as Xara's <a href="/wiki/Xara_Flare" title="Xara Flare">Flare</a> and Sharp's <a href="/wiki/Extended_Vector_Animation" title="Extended Vector Animation">Extended Vector Animation</a> formats. Several developers quickly created a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C_library" title="C library">C library</a> for producing SWF. In February 1999, MorphInk 99 was introduced, the first third-party program to create SWF files. Macromedia also hired <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Middlesoft&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Middlesoft (page does not exist)">Middlesoft</a> to create a freely available <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Development_kit" title="Development kit">developers' kit</a> for the SWF file format versions 3 to 5.</p>
<p>Macromedia made the Flash Files specifications for versions 6 and later available only under a <a href="/wiki/Non-disclosure_agreement" title="Non-disclosure agreement">non-disclosure agreement</a>, but they are widely available from various sites.</p>
<p>In April 2006, the Flash SWF file format specification was released with details on the then newest version format (Flash 8). Although still lacking specific information on the incorporated video compression formats (On2, Sorenson Spark, etc.), this new documentation covered all the new features offered in Flash v8 including new ActionScript commands, expressive filter controls, and so on. The file format specification document is offered only to developers who agree to a license agreement that permits them to use the specifications only to develop programs that can export to the Flash file format. The license does not allow the use of the specifications to create programs that can be used for playback of Flash files. The Flash 9 specification was made available under similar restrictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2009, Adobe launched the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_Screen_Project" title="Open Screen Project">Open Screen Project</a> (<a class="external text" href="https://www.adobe.com/openscreenproject/faq/" rel="nofollow">Adobe link</a>), which made the SWF specification available without restrictions. Previously, developers could not use the specification for making SWF-compatible players, but only for making SWF-exporting authoring software. The specification still omits information on codecs such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sorenson_codec" title="Sorenson codec">Sorenson Spark</a>, however.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Animation_tools">Animation tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Animation tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_tools">Official tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Official tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a> authoring program is primarily used to design graphics and animation and publish the same for websites, web applications, and video games. The program also offers limited support for audio and video embedding, and ActionScript scripting.</p>
<p>Adobe released <a href="/wiki/Adobe_LiveMotion" title="Adobe LiveMotion">Adobe LiveMotion</a>, designed to create interactive animation content and export it to a variety of formats, including SWF. LiveMotion failed to gain any notable user base.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="Statement needs to be more specific about the content to which it refers. (December 2015)">specify</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In February 2003, Macromedia purchased Presedia, which had developed a Flash authoring tool that automatically converted PowerPoint files into Flash. Macromedia subsequently released the new product as Breeze, which included many new enhancements.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Third-party_tools">Third-party tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Third-party tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_vector_graphics_editors" title="Comparison of vector graphics editors">Comparison of vector graphics editors</a></div>
<p>Various free and commercial software packages can output animations into the Flash SWF format, suitable for display on the web, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/SWiSH_Max" title="SWiSH Max">SWiSH Max</a> is an animation editor with preset animation, developed by an ex-employee of Macromedia, that can output Flash animations</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ToonBoom" title="ToonBoom">Toon Boom</a> is a traditional animation tool that can output Flash animations</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> <a href="/wiki/Keynote_(presentation_software)" title="Keynote (presentation software)">Keynote</a> allows users to export presentations to Flash SWF animations</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xara_Photo_%26_Graphic_Designer" title="Xara Photo &amp; Graphic Designer">Xara Photo &amp; Graphic Designer</a> can output Flash animations</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ajax_Animator" title="Ajax Animator">Ajax Animator</a> aim to create a Flash development environment</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KToon" title="KToon">KToon</a> can edit vectors and generate SWF, but its interface is very different from Macromedia's</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Screencast" title="Screencast">Screencast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Screencam" title="Screencam">Screencam</a>, produces demos or tutorials by capturing the screen and generating a Flash animation of the same</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GoAnimate" title="GoAnimate">GoAnimate</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">software as a service</a> tool to create animated videos.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anime_Studio" title="Anime Studio">Anime Studio</a> is a 2D animation software package specialized for character animation, that creates Flash animations</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Question_Writer" title="Question Writer">Question Writer</a> publishes its quizzes to Flash animations</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenOffice.org" title="OpenOffice.org">OpenOffice Impress</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toufee" title="Toufee">Toufee</a></li>
<li>KoolMoves</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Express_Animator" title="Express Animator">Express Animator</a></li>
<li>CelAction2D</li>
<li>Alligator Flash Designer</li>
<li>Amara Web</li>
<li>Clash</li>
<li>Salasaga</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Synfig" title="Synfig">Synfig</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The Flash 4 Linux project was an initiative to develop an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> application as an alternative to <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a>. Development plans included authoring capacity for 2D animation, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tweening" title="Tweening">tweening</a>, as well as outputing SWF file formats. F4L evolved into an editor that was capable of authoring 2D animation and publishing of SWF files. Flash 4 Linux was renamed UIRA. UIRA intended to combine the resources and knowledge of the F4L project and the Qflash project, both of which were Open Source applications that aimed to provide an alternative to the proprietary Adobe Flash.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Programming_tools">Programming tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Programming tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_tools_2">Official tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Official tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Adobe provides a series of tools to develop <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Software_applications" title="Software applications">software applications</a> and <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a> for Flash:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apache_Flex" title="Apache Flex">Apache Flex</a> SDK – a free, open source SDK to compile Flash-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rich_Internet_applications" title="Rich Internet applications">rich Internet applications</a> from source code. The Apache Flex <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> 3.0 compiler generates SWF files from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ActionScript_3" title="ActionScript 3">ActionScript 3</a> files. Flex was the primary ActionScript 3 compiler and was actively developed by Adobe before it was donated to <a href="/wiki/Apache_Software_Foundation" title="Apache Software Foundation">Apache Software Foundation</a> in 2011.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a> – primarily used to design graphics and animation, but supports ActionScript scripting and debugging.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Builder" title="Adobe Flash Builder">Adobe Flash Builder</a> – enterprise application development &amp; debugging, contains the <a href="/wiki/Apache_Flex" title="Apache Flex">Flex SDK</a> with UI and charting components.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Scout" title="Adobe Scout">Adobe Scout</a> – a visual profiler to optimize performance of Flash content.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CrossBridge" title="CrossBridge">CrossBridge</a> – a free SDK to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross_compilation" title="Cross compilation">cross-compile</a> C++ code to run in Flash Player.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Third-party_tools_2">Third-party tools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Third-party tools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Third-party development tools have been created to assist developers in creating software applications and video games with Flash.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/FlashDevelop" title="FlashDevelop">FlashDevelop</a> is a free and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open-source" title="Open-source">open-source</a> Flash <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> IDE, which includes a project manager and debugger for building applications on Flash Player and <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Powerflasher_FDT" title="Powerflasher FDT">Powerflasher FDT</a> is a commercial ActionScript IDE similar to FlashDevelop.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haxe" title="Haxe">Haxe</a> is an open source, high-level object-oriented programming language geared towards web-content creation that can compile SWF files from Haxe programs. As of 2012, <a href="/wiki/Haxe" title="Haxe">Haxe</a> can build programs for Flash Player that perform faster than the same application built with the Adobe Flex SDK compiler, due to additional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compiler_optimization" title="Compiler optimization">compiler optimizations</a> supported in Haxe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (August 2014)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SWFTools" title="SWFTools">SWFTools</a> (specifically, swfc) is an open-source <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> 3.0 compiler which generates SWF files from script files, which includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SVG" title="SVG">SVG</a> tags.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Swfmill" title="Swfmill">swfmill</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTASC" title="MTASC">MTASC</a> also provide tools to create SWF files by compiling text, ActionScript or XML files into <a href="/wiki/Flash_animation" title="Flash animation">Flash animations</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ming_library" title="Ming library">Ming library</a>, to create SWF files programmatically, has interfaces for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C_(Programming_Language)" title="C (Programming Language)">C</a>, <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">Perl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ruby_(programming_language)" title="Ruby (programming language)">Ruby</a>. It is able to import and export graphics from XML into SWF.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proprietary">Proprietary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Proprietary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a> is the multimedia and application player originally developed by <a href="/wiki/Macromedia" title="Macromedia">Macromedia</a> and acquired by <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe Systems</a>. It plays <a href="/wiki/SWF" title="SWF">SWF</a> files, which can be created by <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Animate" title="Adobe Animate">Adobe Animate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apache_Flex" title="Apache Flex">Apache Flex</a>, or a number of other <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe Systems</a> and 3rd party tools. It has support for a scripting language called <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a>, which can be used to display Flash Video from an SWF file.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Scaleform_GFx" title="Scaleform GFx">Scaleform GFx</a> is a commercial alternative Flash player that features fully hardware-accelerated 2D graphics rendering using the <a href="/wiki/Graphics_processing_unit" title="Graphics processing unit">GPU</a>. Scaleform has high conformance with both Flash 10 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ActionScript_3" title="ActionScript 3">ActionScript 3</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ActionScript_3_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-ActionScript_3-52">[51]</a></sup> and Flash 8 ActionScript 2. Scaleform GFx is a game development middleware solution that helps create graphical user interfaces or <a href="/wiki/HUD_(video_gaming)" title="HUD (video gaming)">HUDs</a> within 3D video games. It does not work with web browsers.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/IrfanView" title="IrfanView">IrfanView</a>, an image viewer, uses Flash Player to display SWF files.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_source">Open source</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Open source">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lightspark" title="Lightspark">Lightspark</a> is a free and open source SWF player that supports most of <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> 3.0 and has a <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a>-compatible <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_(computing)" title="Plug-in (computing)">plug-in</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> It will fall back on <a href="/wiki/Gnash_(software)" title="Gnash (software)">Gnash</a>, a free SWF player supporting ActionScript 1.0 and 2.0 (AVM1) code. Lightspark supports <a href="/wiki/OpenGL" title="OpenGL">OpenGL</a>-based rendering for 3D content. The player is also compatible with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H.264" title="H.264">H.264</a> Flash videos on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gnash_(software)" title="Gnash (software)">Gnash</a> aimed to create a software player and browser plugin replacement for the Adobe Flash Player. Gnash can play <a href="/wiki/SWF" title="SWF">SWF</a> files up to version 7, and 80% of <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> 2.0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> Gnash run on Windows, Linux and other platforms for the 32-bit, 64-bit, and other operating systems but the project was terminated in February 2012.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shumway_(software)" title="Shumway (software)">Shumway</a> was an open source Flash Player released by Mozilla in November 2012. It was built in JavaScript and is thus compatible with modern web-browsers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> In early October 2013, Shumway was included by default in the Firefox nightly branch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> Shumway rendered Flash contents by translating contents inside Flash files to <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> elements, and running an <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> interpreter in <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> It supported both AVM1 and AVM2, and ActionScript versions 1, 2, and 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Development of Shumway ceased in early 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a> cannot ship as part of a pure <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a>, or completely free operating system, as its distribution is bound to the <a class="external text" href="http://www.macromedia.com/software/flash/open/licensing/" rel="nofollow">Macromedia Licensing Program</a> and subject to proposition first from Adobe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Availability">Availability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Availability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Desktop_computers">Desktop computers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Desktop computers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flash_Player">Flash Player</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Flash Player">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The latest version of <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a> is available for three major desktop platforms, including <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flashrequirements_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-flashrequirements-62">[61]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> the <a href="/wiki/Google_Native_Client#Pepper" title="Google Native Client">PPAPI</a> plug-in is available, the <a href="/wiki/NPAPI" title="NPAPI">NPAPI</a> version wasn't updated to new major versions for a while,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> until Adobe changed its mind on stopping supporting and its former plan of discontinuing "in 2017".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Adobe Flash Player is available in four flavors:</p>
<ul>
<li>ActiveX-based Plug-in</li>
<li>NPAPI-based Plug-in</li>
<li>PPAPI-based Plug-in</li>
<li>Projector</li>
</ul>
<p>The <i>ActiveX</i> version is an <a href="/wiki/ActiveX" title="ActiveX">ActiveX</a> control for use in <a href="/wiki/Internet_Explorer" title="Internet Explorer">Internet Explorer</a> and any other Windows applications that supports ActiveX technology. The <i>Plug-in</i> versions are available for browsers supporting either <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netscape_Plugin_Application_Programming_Interface" title="Netscape Plugin Application Programming Interface">NPAPI</a> or <a href="/wiki/Google_Native_Client#Pepper" title="Google Native Client">PPAPI</a> plug-ins on <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>. The <i>projector</i> version is a standalone player that can open <a href="/wiki/SWF" title="SWF">SWF</a> files directly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following table documents Flash Player and Adobe AIR support on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desktop_operating_system" title="Desktop operating system">desktop operating systems</a>:</p>

</tr>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adobe_AIR">Adobe AIR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Adobe AIR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The latest version of <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a>, version 18, contains <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a> 18, and is available for <a href="/wiki/Windows_XP" title="Windows XP">Windows XP</a> and later, as well as <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fp11ios_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-fp11ios-69">[68]</a></sup> Official support for desktop Linux distributions ceased in June 2011 with version 2.6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup></p>
