<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_devices">Mobile devices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mobile devices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flash_Player_2">Flash Player</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Flash Player">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player</a> was available for a variety of mobile operating systems, including <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> (between versions 2.2<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> and 4.0.4<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Pocket_PC" title="Pocket PC">Pocket PC</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Windows_CE" title="Windows CE">Windows CE</a>, <a href="/wiki/QNX" title="QNX">QNX</a> (e.g. on <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_PlayBook" title="BlackBerry PlayBook">BlackBerry PlayBook</a>), <a href="/wiki/Symbian" title="Symbian">Symbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_OS" title="Palm OS">Palm OS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/WebOS" title="WebOS">webOS</a> (since version 2.0<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup>). Flash Player for smart phones was made available to handset manufacturers at the end of 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-palmpr_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-palmpr-80">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, in November 2011, Adobe announced the withdrawal of support for Flash Player on mobile devices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfgate_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-sfgate-81">[80]</a></sup> Adobe continues to support deploying Flash-based content as mobile applications via <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a>.</p>
<p>Adobe is reaffirming its commitment to "aggressively contribute" to HTML5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> Adobe announced the end of Flash for mobile platforms or TV, instead focusing on <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> for browser content and <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a> for the various mobile <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_digital_distribution_platforms_for_mobile_devices" title="List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices">application stores</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> and described it as "the beginning of the end".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> BlackBerry LTD (formerly known as RIM) announced that it would continue to develop Flash Player for the PlayBook.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p><span id="Flash_for_iOS"></span>There is no Adobe Flash Player for iOS devices (iPhone, iPad and iPod Touch). However, Flash content can be made to run on iOS devices in a variety of ways:</p>
<ul>
<li>Flash content can be bundled inside an <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a> app, which will then run on iOS devices. (Apple did not allow this for a while, but they relaxed those restrictions in September 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup>)</li>
<li>On March 8, 2011, Techradar reported that Adobe provides an experimental server side tool (<a class="external text" href="http://labs.adobe.com/technologies/wallaby/" rel="nofollow">Wallaby</a>) to convert Flash programs (as far as possible) to HTML5 code, thus allowing iOS devices to display the content.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></li>
<li>If the content is Flash video being served by Adobe Flash Media Server 4.5, the server will translate and send the video as HTTP Dynamic Streaming or HTTP Live Streaming, both of which can be played by iOS devices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li>Some specialized mobile browsers manage to accommodate Flash via streaming content from the cloud directly to a user's device. Some examples are Photon Browser<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> and Puffin Web Browser.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The mobile version of <a href="/wiki/Internet_Explorer" title="Internet Explorer">Internet Explorer</a> for <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a> cannot play Flash content,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> however Flash support is still present on the <a href="/wiki/Windows_RT" title="Windows RT">tablet version of Windows</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adobe_AIR_2">Adobe AIR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Adobe AIR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ambox_current_red.svg"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(March 2016)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a> was released in 2008, and allows the creation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_application" title="Mobile application">mobile applications</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile games</a> using Flash and <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a>. Notable mobile games built with Flash include <i><a href="/wiki/Angry_Birds" title="Angry Birds">Angry Birds</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Machinarium" title="Machinarium">Machinarium</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Defend_Your_Castle" title="Defend Your Castle">Defend Your Castle</a></i>.</p>
<p>Using AIR, developers can access the full Adobe Flash functionality, including <a href="/wiki/Text_file" title="Text file">text</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vector_graphics" title="Vector graphics">vector graphics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raster_graphics" title="Raster graphics">raster graphics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_video" title="Digital video">video</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_audio" title="Digital audio">audio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_camera" title="Digital camera">camera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microphone" title="Microphone">microphone</a> capability. Adobe AIR also includes additional features such as file system integration, native client extensions, <a href="/wiki/Desktop_environment" title="Desktop environment">desktop</a> integration and access to connected devices and sensors.</p>
<p>AIR applications can be published as native phone applications on certain mobile operating systems, such as <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> (<a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A8" title="ARM Cortex-A8">ARM Cortex-A8</a> and above<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flashmobileblog1_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-flashmobileblog1-97">[96]</a></sup>) and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fp11ios_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-fp11ios-69">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following table explains to what extent Adobe AIR can run on various <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">mobile operating systems</a>:</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable">
<tr>

<th>AIR Framework</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a></td>
<td>Android 2.3+, <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A8" title="ARM Cortex-A8">ARM Cortex-A8</a>+<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> or Android x86<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup></td>
<td>AIR 3.6.0.597 (uses Flash Player 11.6)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-helpx.adobe.com_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-helpx.adobe.com-100">[99]</a></sup></td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portable_electronic_devices">Portable electronic devices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Portable electronic devices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Lite" title="Adobe Flash Lite">Adobe Flash Lite</a> is a lightweight version of Adobe Flash Player intended for mobile phones and other portable electronic devices like <a href="/wiki/Chumby" title="Chumby">Chumby</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IRiver" title="IRiver">iRiver</a>.</p>
<p>On the emerging <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_single-board_computers" title="List of single-board computers">single-board</a> enthusiast market, as substantially popularized by the <a href="/wiki/Raspberry_Pi" title="Raspberry Pi">Raspberry Pi</a>, support from Adobe is lacking. However, the open-source player <a href="/wiki/Gnash_(software)" title="Gnash (software)">Gnash</a> has been ported and found to be useful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Screen_Project">Open Screen Project</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Open Screen Project">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On May 1, 2008, Adobe announced the <i>Open Screen Project</i>, with the intent of providing a consistent application interface across devices such as personal computers, <a href="/wiki/Mobile_device" title="Mobile device">mobile devices</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-osppr_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-osppr-108">[107]</a></sup> When the project was announced, seven goals were outlined: the abolition of licensing fees for Adobe Flash Player and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adobe_Integrated_Runtime" title="Adobe Integrated Runtime">Adobe Integrated Runtime</a>, the removal of restrictions on the use of the <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Shockwave" title="Adobe Shockwave">Shockwave</a> Flash (<a href="/wiki/SWF" title="SWF">SWF</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Flash_Video" title="Flash Video">Flash Video</a> (FLV) <a href="/wiki/File_format" title="File format">file formats</a>, the publishing of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Application_Programming_Interface" title="Application Programming Interface">application programming interfaces</a> for porting Flash to new devices, and the publishing of The Flash Cast protocol and Action Message Format (AMF), which let Flash applications receive information from remote databases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-osppr_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-osppr-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of February 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the specifications removing the restrictions on the use of SWF and FLV/F4V specs have been published.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interview_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-interview-109">[108]</a></sup> The Flash Cast protocol—now known as the Mobile Content Delivery Protocol—and AMF protocols have also been made available,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interview_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-interview-109">[108]</a></sup> with AMF available as an open source implementation, <a href="/wiki/BlazeDS" title="BlazeDS">BlazeDS</a>.</p>
<p>The list of mobile device providers who have joined the project includes <a href="/wiki/Palm,_Inc." title="Palm, Inc.">Palm</a>, Motorola, and Nokia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> who, together with Adobe, have announced a $10 million Open Screen Project fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Open Screen Project is no longer accepting new applications according to partner BSQuare. However paid licensing is still an option for device makers who want to use Adobe software.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_support">Mobile support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Mobile support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Websites built with Adobe Flash will not function on most modern mobile devices running <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_Android" title="Google Android">Google Android</a> or <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> (<a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a>). The only alternative is using <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> and <a href="/wiki/Responsive_web_design" title="Responsive web design">responsive web design</a> to build websites that support both desktop and mobile devices.</p>
<p>However, Flash is still actively used to build mobile games using <a href="/wiki/Adobe_AIR" title="Adobe AIR">Adobe AIR</a>. Such games will not work in mobile web browsers, but must be installed via the appropriate <a href="/wiki/App_store" title="App store">app store</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternatives">Alternatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Alternatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HTML5">HTML5</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: HTML5">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_HTML5_and_Flash" title="Comparison of HTML5 and Flash">Comparison of HTML5 and Flash</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> is often cited as an alternative to Adobe Flash technology usage on web pages. Adobe released a tool that converts Flash to <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> and in June 2011, Google released an experimental tool that does the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> In January 2015, <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> defaulted to HTML5 players to better support more devices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms">Criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vendor_dependence">Vendor dependence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Vendor dependence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Vendor_lock-in" title="Vendor lock-in">Vendor lock-in</a></div>
<p>The reliance on Adobe for decoding Flash makes its use on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> a concern—the completeness of its public specifications are debated, and no complete implementation of Flash is publicly available in <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> form with a license that permits reuse. Generally, public specifications are what makes a format re-implementable (see <a href="/wiki/Future_proof#Data_storage" title="Future proof">future proofing data storage</a>), and reusable codebases can be <a href="/wiki/Software_portability" title="Software portability">ported</a> to new platforms without the endorsement of the format creator.</p>
<p>Adobe's restrictions on the use of the SWF/FLV specifications were lifted in February 2009 (see <a href="#Open_Screen_Project">Adobe's Open Screen Project</a>). However, despite efforts of projects like <a href="/wiki/Gnash_(software)" title="Gnash (software)">Gnash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swfdec" title="Swfdec">Swfdec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lightspark" title="Lightspark">Lightspark</a>, a complete free Flash player is yet to be seen, as of September 2011. For example, Gnash cannot use SWF v10 yet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> Notably, Gnash has been a long-standing high priority project of the <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">Free Software Foundation</a> since at least 2007, and it was ranked number one in September 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable advocates of free software, open standards, and the World Wide Web have warned against the use of Flash:</p>
<p>Founder of <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Europe" title="Mozilla Europe">Mozilla Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tristan_Nitot" title="Tristan Nitot">Tristan Nitot</a> stated in 2008:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>Companies building websites should beware of proprietary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rich-media" title="Rich-media">rich-media</a> technologies like Adobe's Flash and Microsoft's Silverlight. (...) You're producing content for your users and there's someone in the middle deciding whether users should see your content.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Representing open standards, inventor of <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" title="Cascading Style Sheets">CSS</a> and co-author of <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A5kon_Wium_Lie" title="Håkon Wium Lie">Håkon Wium Lie</a> explained in a <a href="/wiki/AtGoogleTalks" title="AtGoogleTalks">Google tech talk</a> of 2007, entitled "the &lt;video&gt; element", the proposal of <a href="/wiki/Theora" title="Theora">Theora</a> as the format for <a href="/wiki/HTML5_video" title="HTML5 video">HTML5 video</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>I believe very strongly, that we need to agree on some kind of baseline video format if [the video element] is going to succeed. Flash is today the baseline format on the web. The problem with Flash is that it's not an open standard.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Representing the <a href="/wiki/Free_software_movement" title="Free software movement">free software movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stallman" title="Richard Stallman">Richard Stallman</a> stated in a speech in 2004 that:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> "The use of Flash in websites is a major problem for our community."</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accessibility">Accessibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Accessibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Usability consultant <a href="/wiki/Jakob_Nielsen_(usability_consultant)" title="Jakob Nielsen (usability consultant)">Jakob Nielsen</a> published an Alertbox in 2000 entitled, <i>Flash: 99% Bad</i>, stating that "Flash tends to degrade websites for three reasons: it encourages design abuse, it breaks with the Web's fundamental interaction principles, and it distracts attention from the site's core value."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Some problems have been at least partially fixed since Nielsen's complaints: Text size can be controlled using full page zoom and it has been possible for authors to include alternative text in Flash since Flash Player 6.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flash_blocking_in_web_browsers">Flash blocking in web browsers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Flash blocking in web browsers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Noflash.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="206" data-file-width="300" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ca/Noflash.png/220px-Noflash.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/ca/Noflash.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Noflash.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Some websites rely heavily on Flash and become unusable without Flash Player, or with Flash blocked</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Flash content is usually embedded using the <code>object</code> or <code>embed</code> <a href="/wiki/HTML_element" title="HTML element">HTML element</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> A web browser that does not fully implement one of these elements displays the replacement text, if supplied by the web page. Often, a plugin is required for the browser to fully implement these elements, though some users cannot or will not install it.</p>
<p>Since Flash can be used to produce content (such as advertisements) that some users find obnoxious or take a large amount of bandwidth to download, some web browsers default to not play Flash content before the user clicks on it, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Konqueror" title="Konqueror">Konqueror</a>, <a href="/wiki/K-Meleon" title="K-Meleon">K-Meleon</a>.</p>
<p>Most current browsers have a feature to block plugins, playing one only when the user clicks it. Opera versions since 10.5 feature native Flash blocking. Opera Turbo requires the user to click to play Flash content, and the browser also allows the user to enable this option permanently. Both Chrome<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> and Firefox<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> have an option to enable "click to play plugins". Equivalent "Flash blocker" extensions are also available for many popular browsers: Firefox has <a href="/wiki/Flashblock" title="Flashblock">Flashblock</a> and <a href="/wiki/NoScript" title="NoScript">NoScript</a>, Internet Explorer has Foxie, which contains a number of features, one of them named Flashblock. WebKit-based browsers under macOS, such as Apple's Safari, have ClickToFlash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> <span id="Security"></span> In June 2015, Google announced that Chrome will "pause" advertisements and "non-central" Flash content by default.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a> (from version 46) rewrites old Flash-only <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> embed code into YouTube's modern embedded player that is capable of using either <a href="/wiki/HTML5_video" title="HTML5 video">HTML5</a> or Flash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firefox_embed_rewrite_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-firefox_embed_rewrite-127">[126]</a></sup> Such embed code is used by non-YouTube sites to embed YouTube's videos, and can still be encountered for example on old blogs and forums.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player#Security" title="Adobe Flash Player">Adobe Flash Player § Security</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Browser_security#Plugins_and_extensions" title="Browser security">Browser security § Plugins and extensions</a></div>
<p>For many years Adobe Flash Player's security record<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> has led many security experts to recommend against installing the player, or to block Flash content.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Computer_Emergency_Readiness_Team" title="United States Computer Emergency Readiness Team">US-CERT</a> has recommended blocking Flash,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> and security researcher <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Miller_(security_researcher)" title="Charlie Miller (security researcher)">Charlie Miller</a> recommended "not to install Flash";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> however, for people still using Flash, <a href="/wiki/Intego" title="Intego">Intego</a> recommended that users get trusted updates "only directly from the vendor that publishes them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> As of February 12, 2015, Adobe Flash Player has over 400 <a href="/wiki/Common_Vulnerabilities_and_Exposures" title="Common Vulnerabilities and Exposures">CVE</a> entries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> of which over 300 lead to <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_code_execution" title="Arbitrary code execution">arbitrary code execution</a>, and past vulnerabilities have enabled spying via web cameras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FlashSettings_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FlashSettings-137">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> Security experts have long predicted the demise of Flash, saying that with the rise of HTML5 <i>"....the need for browser plugins such as Flash is diminishing"</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> as only 7 to 10 percent of websites still use it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newman_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-newman-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>Active moves by third-parties to limit the risk began with <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> in 2010 saying that Apple would not allow Flash on the <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPod_touch" title="IPod touch">iPod touch</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a> - citing abysmal security as one reason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thoughtsFlash_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-thoughtsFlash-142">[141]</a></sup> In July 2015, a series of newly discovered vulnerabilities resulted in <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>'s chief security officer, Alex Stamos, issuing a call to Adobe to discontinue the software entirely<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stamos_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-stamos-143">[142]</a></sup> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozilla_Firefox" title="Mozilla Firefox">Mozilla Firefox</a> web browser, <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Safari_(web_browser)" title="Safari (web browser)">Apple Safari</a> to blacklist all earlier versions of Flash Player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars-flashblockfirefox_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-ars-flashblockfirefox-144">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flashblocksafari_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-flashblocksafari-147">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a result, "Adobe has essentially stopped trying to do anything new and innovative with Flash."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newman_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-newman-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flash_cookies">Flash cookies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_Flash&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Flash cookies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Local_shared_object" title="Local shared object">Local shared object</a></div>
<p>Like the <a href="/wiki/HTTP_cookie" title="HTTP cookie">HTTP cookie</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_cookie" title="Flash cookie">flash cookie</a> (also known as a “<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_Shared_Object" title="Local Shared Object">Local Shared Object</a>”) can be used to save application data. Flash cookies are not shared across <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domains</a>. An August 2009 study by the <a href="/wiki/Ashkan_Soltani" title="Ashkan Soltani">Ashkan Soltani</a> and a team of researchers at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley">UC Berkeley</a> found that 50% of websites using Flash were also employing flash cookies, yet privacy policies rarely disclosed them, and user controls for <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash_Player#Privacy" title="Adobe Flash Player">privacy preferences</a> were lacking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> Most browsers' cache and history suppress or delete functions did not affect Flash Player's writing Local Shared Objects to its own cache in version 10.2 and earlier, at which point the user community was much less aware of the existence and function of Flash cookies than HTTP cookies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> Thus, users with those versions, having deleted HTTP cookies and purged browser history files and caches, may believe that they have purged all tracking data from their computers when in fact Flash browsing history remains. Adobe's own Flash <a class="external text" href="http://www.macromedia.com/support/documentation/en/flashplayer/help/settings_manager07.html" rel="nofollow">Website Storage Settings panel</a>, a submenu of Adobe's Flash <a class="external text" href="http://www.macromedia.com/support/documentation/en/flashplayer/help/settings_manager.html" rel="nofollow">Settings Manager web application</a>, and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_Shared_Object#Editors_and_toolkits" title="Local Shared Object">editors and toolkits</a> can manage settings for and delete Flash Local Shared Objects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-test-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-test_14-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="https://speedtest.net" rel="nofollow">See tests completed on page.</a></span></li>
